https://download.agiv.be/Producten/Detail?id=3894&title=Wegenregister_21_09_2017

data pdf states:

```
Veld 13 Linkerstraatnaam
veldnaam LSTRNM
definitie Straatnaam volgens CRAB, voorkomend aan de linkerstraatkant
soort Beschrijvend
datatype Tekst(80)
domein nvt
conditie Verplicht
```
and RSTRNM
```
definitie Straatnaam volgens CRAB, voorkomend aan de rechterstraatkant
soort Beschrijvend
datatype Tekst(80)
domein nvt
conditie Verplicht
```
For starters, many are empty, unlike the data def says : 'conditie verplicht'
They can be the same, but also missing.  when I take a few and go look at the osm map, I can't make sense of it.

# mapping the entities to the OSM equivalent
 	sed -e 's/LBLTYPE/building/g;s/OIDN/source:geometry:oidn/g;s/UIDN/source:geometry:uidn/g;s/OPNDATUM/source:geometry:date/g;s/hoofdgebouw/house/g;s/bijgebouw/shed/g;s/tag k=\"TYPE\"\sv=\"[0-9]\+\"/tag k="source:geometry:entity" v="Gbg"/g' -i "filename.osm"
    # this line is needed for the tools to work so we need to add it to the osm file using sed to replace
 	sed -e 's/ visible="true"/ version="1" timestamp="1970-01-01T00:00:01Z" changeset="1" visible="true"/g' -i "filename.osm"`

Tue, Nov 21, 2017, 13:08:38 - @gplv2:matrix.org: bebot: help
Tue, Nov 21, 2017, 13:08:38 - bebot: BEBOT adapter - Reply with the adapter
BEBOT animate me <query> - The same thing as `image me`, except adds a few parameters to try to return an animated GIF instead.
BEBOT changeset <number> - Blame someone
BEBOT echo <text> - Reply back with <text>
BEBOT help - Displays all of the help commands that this bot knows about.
BEBOT help <query> - Displays all help commands that match <query>.
BEBOT hotshots [now|today] - shows the active 10 mappers of the moment or by total of the day
BEBOT image me <query> - The Original. Queries Google Images for <query> and returns a random top result.
BEBOT map me <query> - Returns a map view of the area returned by `query`.
BEBOT mustache me <url|query> - Adds a mustache to the specified URL or query result.
BEBOT ping - Reply with pong
BEBOT pug bomb N - get N pugs
BEBOT pug me - Receive a pug
BEBOT stats <postcode> - Shows you a count for the number of streets in that postcode
BEBOT streetmap <postcode> [partialstring] [cycle|mapnik] - creates a static image given by the bounds of the street we search
BEBOT streets <postcode> [partialstring] - searches for streetlist in postcode
BEBOT the rules - Make sure hubot still knows the rules.
BEBOT time - Reply with current time
BEBOT translate me <phrase> - Searches for a translation for the <phrase> and then prints that bad boy out.
BEBOT translate me from <source> into <target> <phrase> - Translates <phrase> from <source> into <target>. Both <source> and <target> are optional
author Glenn Plas for OSM.BE
ship it - Display a motivation squirrel

Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:19:52 - @gplv2:matrix.org: that was the error
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:20:35 - @gplv2:matrix.org: ```
...
 FROM public.permit_request_t permit
     JOIN public.case_t c ON permit.id = c.id
     LEFT JOIN public.delivery_t del ON permit.delivery_id = del.id
     LEFT JOIN public.permit_t p ON permit.id = del.id
...

has to be:
...
   FROM public.permit_request_t permit
     JOIN public.case_t c ON permit.id = c.id
     LEFT JOIN public.delivery_t del ON permit.delivery_id = del.id
     LEFT JOIN public.permit_t p ON permit.id = p.id
```
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:20:50 - @gplv2:matrix.org: last line of both
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:21:03 - @gplv2:matrix.org: first does a join but fails to reuse the table alias
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:21:34 - @gplv2:matrix.org: but del is a alias elsewhere in the view (it's really like 5 pages long, it's terrible)
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:21:55 - @gplv2:matrix.org: so it becomes cartesian product-by-typo
Tue, Feb 20, 2018, 15:22:12 - @gplv2:matrix.org: onyl 38 JOIN's btw in that query ...

Tue, Mar 6, 2018, 20:39:18 - @gplv2:matrix.org: This is quite fast :
Tue, Mar 6, 2018, 20:39:22 - @gplv2:matrix.org: ```
SELECT
        building,
        landuse,
        ST_Area(way) AS size,
        St_Intersects(way,
        ST_SetSRID(ST_GeomFromGeoJSON('{"type":"Polygon","coordinates":[[[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619],[497426.60277452,6617054.89041791],[497430.365373307,6617052.92797032],[497439.62715494,6617048.08373234],[497440.072432905,6617047.8538963],[497440.094696803,6617047.88925568],[497444.024274828,6617055.35009039],[497445.838782529,6617054.60754255],[497449.979867585,6617054.90809762],[497452.473424179,6617059.82305852],[497451.193250034,6617060.53024738],[497454.621890351,6617066.87727012],[497446.54009532,6617071.04968887],[497440.673558154,6617074.07292581],[497430.009150936,6617079.5890101],[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619]]]}'),
        900913)) AS intersects 
    FROM
        planet_osm_polygon 
    WHERE
        (
            St_Contains(way, ST_SetSRID(ST_GeomFromGeoJSON('{"type":"Polygon","coordinates":[[[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619],[497426.60277452,6617054.89041791],[497430.365373307,6617052.92797032],[497439.62715494,6617048.08373234],[497440.072432905,6617047.8538963],[497440.094696803,6617047.88925568],[497444.024274828,6617055.35009039],[497445.838782529,6617054.60754255],[497449.979867585,6617054.90809762],[497452.473424179,6617059.82305852],[497451.193250034,6617060.53024738],[497454.621890351,6617066.87727012],[497446.54009532,6617071.04968887],[497440.673558154,6617074.07292581],[497430.009150936,6617079.5890101],[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619]]]}'), 900913)) 
            OR St_Intersects(way, ST_SetSRID(ST_GeomFromGeoJSON('{"type":"Polygon","coordinates":[[[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619],[497426.60277452,6617054.89041791],[497430.365373307,6617052.92797032],[497439.62715494,6617048.08373234],[497440.072432905,6617047.8538963],[497440.094696803,6617047.88925568],[497444.024274828,6617055.35009039],[497445.838782529,6617054.60754255],[497449.979867585,6617054.90809762],[497452.473424179,6617059.82305852],[497451.193250034,6617060.53024738],[497454.621890351,6617066.87727012],[497446.54009532,6617071.04968887],[497440.673558154,6617074.07292581],[497430.009150936,6617079.5890101],[497419.300215922,6617058.70923619]]]}'), 900913))
        ) 
        AND (
            landuse IS NOT NULL 
            OR building IS NOT NULL
        ) 
    ORDER BY
        size LIMIT 3
```

Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:22:44 - @gplv2:matrix.org: I add it
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:22:54 - @gplv2:matrix.org: it's in that script code I've sent you :)
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:23:06 - @gplv2:matrix.org: things like verdieping
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:23:24 - @gplv2:matrix.org: they usually are houses (with road under it for parking for example)
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:24:07 - @gplv2:matrix.org: so min_building level etc applies, but I don't want this to go automatically, the fixmes and notes are to trigger JOSM warnings, so a human can look at it, works pretty well actually.
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:25:43 - @gplv2:matrix.org: here are the fixme's :
Wed, Mar 7, 2018, 11:25:47 - @gplv2:matrix.org: ```
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET fixme='verdieping, correct the building tag, add building:level and building:min_level before upload in JOSM!', building='yes' where building='verdieping';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET building='yes', man_made='water_tower' WHERE building='watertoren';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='tower', "tower:type"='cooling' , building='yes' WHERE building='koeltoren';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET building='',tags=hstore('building:part', 'yes'), foot='designated', layer='1', fixme='This is a walking bridge between buildings, please review and complete all tags, use way osmid 118022697 as example' WHERE building='loopbrug';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='chimney', building='', fixme='Add the chimney type and optionally building in case the chimney is part of a building' WHERE building='schoorsteen';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='works', building='' , fixme='This installation is chemical in nature, refine where possible by adding a product=* tag' WHERE building='chemische installatie';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='pier', building='' , fixme='This is a havendam, which should be a pier, make sure to verify this' WHERE building='havendam';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='mast', building='' , fixme='This is a mast , either high voltage powerline or public TV broadcast, refine this with power, tower:type, height tags or/and communication:* namespace tags, see wiki for more' WHERE building='hoogspanningsmast / openbare TV mast';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='storage_tank', building='', fixme='Add the silo type and optionally building type, refine this with content=* see wiki for more information' WHERE building='silo, opslagtank';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='groyne', building='', fixme='This can be either: golfbreker, strandhoofd of lage havendam' WHERE building='golfbreker, strandhoofd en lage havendam';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='bridge', building='' WHERE building='overbrugging';
UPDATE planet_osm_polygon SET man_made='weir', fixme='Waterbouwkundig constructie: Doublecheck this tag carefully, it can be a weir, lock_gate, dam etc. check the wiki for the waterways key for more information. When in doubt, delete this object', building='' WHERE building='waterbouwkundig constructie';
```

Fri, Apr 6, 2018, 23:29:21 - @gplv2:matrix.org: well, json is a notation, in fact it's programming code, it's a javascript way of defining multidimensional data structure.  In essence they are equal, but logically JSON doesn't have any requirements other than that it needs to be semantically correct.  geojson requires a certain format (aka schema) so it's like a more strict in how it should look like.  Both are always json

Fri, Apr 6, 2018, 23:38:18 - @gplv2:matrix.org: GeoJSON is a spec for representing geospatial data in JSON format.  so there is no general-purpose JSON-to-GeoJSON converter because generic JSON contains arbitrary data.  If you want to convert this, it will need a specific script to extract the geojson parts and combine them somehow to make it consumable for QGIS

I've seen bigger prices, in 2009  I got an invoice from google for 30K euro's to perform geocoding request for 800 tracked units.  We had 3500 assets on GPS. Tue, Apr 23, 2019, 15:57:39 - @gplv2:matrix.org: less than 3 seconds in postgis ;-)
Tue, Apr 23, 2019, 16:19:47 - @gplv2:matrix.org: ```
SELECT
        row_to_json(fc)
    FROM
        ( SELECT
            'FeatureCollection' As type,
            array_to_json(array_agg(f)) As features
        FROM
            (SELECT
                'Feature' As type ,
                ST_AsGeoJSON(ST_ConcaveHull(ST_Collect(lg.geom), 0.99))::json As geometry,
                row_to_json((SELECT l FROM (SELECT code_posta) As l )) As properties
             FROM addresses As lg
             WHERE code_posta IS NOT NULL
             GROUP by code_posta
            ) As f )  As fc;
```

Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 19:09:41 - @gplv2:matrix.org: spatialite is also an option
Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 19:10:00 - @gplv2:matrix.org: https://www.gaia-gis.it/fossil/libspatialite/index
Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 19:10:14 - @gplv2:matrix.org: works alsmost exactly like postgis.
Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 19:10:51 - @gplv2:matrix.org: For overpass query :  http://overpass-turbo.eu/s/Iet

Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 19:12:27 - @gplv2:matrix.org: But the postal code thing, there is no flemish town where a postal code is fully embedded in another one.  hence I do doubt a bit about the results in general

Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 21:10:32 - lionel_giard: I also used spatialite before, but since QGIS 3.xx i switched entirely to the new format. Geopackage seems to be superior to spatialite (both are SQLite based) - as it is a geographic standard from the OGC (while spatialite is just a spatial format among others). It is designed to replace shapefile a the defacto standard when doing spatial analysis... It's new but modern and get all the bonus from spatialite + some others things. And if you use QGIS, you'll find that the processing speed is multiple times faster when using geopackage than any other format (as it is optimised for it) - and you can directly save into the existing database when outputing results. So it makes data processing easier than ever - and also exchanging the dataset as it is one file (like spatialite). 
Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 21:12:26 - lionel_giard: Wave can base ourself on the existing postal code of the Brabant Wallon too (they seem to be correct at least when i compared them to the concave/convex hull...).
Wed, Apr 24, 2019, 21:14:30 - lionel_giard: (btw one good advantage of geopackage is that you can delete column in the attribute table more easily than spatialite -> you don't need some tricks to do it ^^)

Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 15:31:12 - @gplv2:matrix.org: Since I know a thing or 2 about track and trace hardware.   It's the firmware that triggers the sample, let me put it this way, instead of having a clock trigger and save a GPS sample, you save samples based on changes in the GPS feed, distance travelled, angle change.  I'm saying that this is a simple stuff, I'm used to professional devices though.  I'm a bit biased.  It's not new though, in 2006 I designed a solution like that, still running.  I have a Garmin Etrex too since probably 2003, it's a simple receiver indeed, but attach it to a computer and with a bit of sofware, it's easy to throw away redundant points a keep a nice track based on the data of the feed.   I really hate spidering on a map if you haven't already noticed
Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 15:34:46 - @gplv2:matrix.org: to me a GPS receiver is the chip btw.   That doesn't go beepbeep
Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 16:07:25 - @_oftc_Stereo:matrix.org: I tend to configure my things to record a point as often as possible - once per second maybe. That way, I don't get cut corners.
Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 16:07:47 - @_oftc_Stereo:matrix.org: The 'smart' sampling, in my experience, cuts corners
Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 16:08:12 - @_oftc_Stereo:matrix.org: Maybe that's changed, but it's a few kb extra for each file, and that's cheap
Sun, Aug 18, 2019, 21:25:00 - @gplv2:matrix.org: I get that for 1 device it's the way to go.  I'm dealing with thousands of GPS trackers, which , if they all generated data like that, it's a lot of data to store, and this is in a database, not a file.  And most of it is useless.  vehicles stand still more time than they move.  The event based approach is quite advanced though.   Corners are fine, if you select the right angles,  I also have G-sensors, and start/stops, speed events,   And all sorts of combinations, like below 30km/h : take a sample every 5 meters, above: take a sample every 500meter (highways) etc.  But I agree if for personal use, you like to get as much as you can.  The only problem sometimes with that aproach is that GPS fixes might fail and/or be of lower quality, which makes your route (if all samples would be displayed on a map) make funny jumps.   That's something customers really don't like, although it can be explained.   Also, it's aheadache to filter out timers when a vehicle stands still, since none of the points are on the same spot due to the inaccuracy in the GPS data (deliberately).

Find two sources of inaccurate position : 1/ sideways - especially in urban canyons, but also in areas with trees and 2/ the unit's position runs behind, by like 20m in open rural areas, but up to 60m in coniferous forests. 

Wed, Aug 21, 2019, 13:39:00 - @koninklijke:matrix.org: Enabling WAAS / EGNOS doesn't really improve things, and there's little difference between the three recording settings 'auto', 'time' and 'distance' : auto tends to add a dozen waypoints close together on some bends, but just one point on other bends - even it it happens to be the same way but in different direction, while time seems to average out the past couple of positions, number of positions used to average seems to depend on clear horizon or again coniferous forest.

The intended route being one based on filtering Mapillary to show which ways haven't been pictured in the past five, three or two years. 

Wed, Aug 21, 2019, 13:40:29 - @koninklijke:matrix.org: More accurate GPS would help in two ways : 3/ better accuracy when geotagging photos for Mapillary and 4/ track that's more in line with reality when improving for example winding forest paths. 

Galileo is the buzzword, understand there are two signals : the GPS L1 / Galileo E1 - which promise in the order of 3 to 5 m accuracy (but deliver errors up to 30m), and Galileo E5a which some sources promise will be better than 1m, others promise 30cm accuracy - take that with a pinch of salt, would still be a huge improvement over the current unit's 'guestimate'. 

Wed, Aug 21, 2019, 13:40:42 - @koninklijke:matrix.org: Smartphones and tablets using the Galileo signal are listed on https://www.usegalileo.eu/EN/inner.html#data=smartphone , wearables and sport devices will be shown by picking another radio button on that page.

Fri, Oct 4, 2019, 17:23:15 - joost_schouppe: Anyone who understands CURL/swagger? I'm trying to get a GeoJSON with all the tasks and their status from Maproulette task 2789 , and that should be possible directlu now. But I have no idea what the hell I'm doing. More info here: https://github.com/osmlab/maproulette3/issues/914
Fri, Oct 4, 2019, 18:54:04 - Jonathan: joost_schouppe: You can make the same request work!
BUT you should use HTTPS or tell cURL to "follow" the redirection between HTTP and HTTPS by adding the `-L` flag!

So:
```
curl -X GET "https://maproulette.org/api/v2/challenge/2789/tasks?limit=0" -H "accept: application/json" -H "content-type: application/json" -o "c2789.txt"
```
or
```
curl -L -X GET "http://maproulette.org/api/v2/challenge/2789/tasks?limit=0" -H "accept: application/json" -H "content-type: application/json" -o "c2789.txt"
```

Mon, Dec 16, 2019, 19:31:28 - escada: grep -> grab / search
| is pass to next statement
so search for "name" in the geojson file, 
pass the result to a sort command 
-u mean keep unique result
pass to "word count" aka wc
-l only counts the number of lines

yes: that is the content of the changeset.
but when there is a bunch of nodes in that changeset, you do not have a lot of context by looking at the text alone.
you might see that node such or such was moved. But you won't know which ways are impacted by that. (if any).

Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 12:19:36 - joost_schouppe: Am I right that TMS is faster than WMTS? Because I hear that WMTS is "more advanced" than TMS
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 13:36:10 - timcouwelier: Not sure if there's a speed difference
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 13:36:19 - timcouwelier: In fact, I'm not sure if I use a TMS for anything
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 13:36:46 - timcouwelier: XYZ seems the more common option for serving tiles
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 13:37:43 - timcouwelier: and I think (but note I'm no expert) WMTS has an advantage over WMS when it comes to caching tiles, which matters a lot if panning around a lot, only have to request the non-cached tiles instead of the whole thing again.
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 13:38:20 - timcouwelier: In GIS, I mostly go for the WMS, but set Qgis to request it only in 512x512 pixel tiles, in case I need large areas at once
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:49:19 - Jonathan: No, not really.
Standard used has nothing to do with the speed. :)

TMS is similar to XYZ (the way OSM tiles are served) : each tile has a coordinate (X, Y, Zoom Level) and an url point to each individual tile (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiled_web_map)

WMTS is "between" TMS/XYZ and WMS.
You can request the WMTS service to give you the list of layers available, query the objects, ... (all of those are not provided by TMS/XYZ) (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_Map_Tile_Service).
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:50:42 - Jonathan: Different technologies for different usage.
If you only need to server a baselayer (like OSM do), go for TMS/XYZ.
If you need a more complex service with layers, queries, ... go for WMTS/WMS.
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:51:33 - Jonathan: Speed is (mostly) only a matter of pre-rendered (or cached) tiles.
And it's possible with WMS, WMTS, TMS, and XYZ.
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:51:46 - joost_schouppe: ah, makes sense
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:52:10 - joost_schouppe: so it is really logical that basemaps are much more often in TMS than WMTS, as you don't need advanced features there
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:52:18 - Jonathan: <@joost_schouppe:matrix.org "so it is really logical that bas..."> Yep :)
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:52:39 - joost_schouppe: so it's not like WMTS is going to replace TMS
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:52:48 - Jonathan: Nope, different usage :)
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:55:00 - joost_schouppe: ok, merci!
Wed, Dec 16, 2020, 14:55:07 - Jonathan: Graag gedaan :D

Ook heb ik een lijst van verkeersborden in het project staan (SimpleFeatureUtils) om op te filteren. Dat was nodig omdat we voor het project alleen gekeken hebben naar verkeersborden die de snelheid beÃ¯nvloeden.

Tue, Jan 11, 2022, 18:00:55 - @gplv2:matrix.org: ```
var inter = mturf.intersect(featureA,featureB);
var overlapsize = mturf.area(inter);
var areasizeA = mturf.area(featureA);
var areasizeB = mturf.area(featureB);
var maxarea = (areasizeA > areasizeB) ? areasizeA : areasizeB;
var overlappct = ( overlapsize / maxarea) * 100;
var perc_overlap = Math.round(( overlappct  + Number.EPSILON) * 100) / 100;

if (perc_overlap > 0.8 ) {
 console.log("features overlap - properties: ");
```
